  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_01e8a4b2-95de-43a0-b5f6-731862580fff'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yeah! I actually read the last book (Mercy Close) in the "Series" first & fell in love with Marian Keyes' writing. It probably helps if you read it in<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">â€¦more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yeah! I actually read the last book (Mercy Close) in the "Series" first &amp; fell in love with Marian Keyes' writing. It probably helps if you read it in order, you'll probably get a little more out of it - but honestly they're all so good even as stand-alones that it didn't matter to me<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3574972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5056211881838499684">After reading this book I decided that I will probably never loan it out because I will want to read it over and over again.<br/><br/>This is, by far, the most emotionally provocative book I've ever read. For about the first 25 chapters or so, I was convinced I knew what was going on, only to be hurled into an entire weekend of crying and page-turning. I couldn't stop crying, yet I couldn't put it down. <br/><br/>This book made me realize so many things about myself, life, death, and what it really and truly means </span>
  <span id="freeText5056211881838499684" style="display:none">After reading this book I decided that I will probably never loan it out because I will want to read it over and over again.<br /><br />This is, by far, the most emotionally provocative book I've ever read. For about the first 25 chapters or so, I was convinced I knew what was going on, only to be hurled into an entire weekend of crying and page-turning. I couldn't stop crying, yet I couldn't put it down. <br /><br />This book made me realize so many things about myself, life, death, and what it really and truly means to love someone so completely that you would be nothing without them.<br /><br />Now, I plan to read all of Marian Keyes' other books. She is an amazingly gifted writer and I can't wait to learn more about the Walsh sisters and the many other characters she's created.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_157042736" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157042736" />
    <a title="Corey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3699250-corey"><img alt="Corey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1276345111p2/3699250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157042736?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corey" href="/user/show/3699250-corey">Corey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141019376" href="/book/show/848752.Anybody_Out_There_">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157042736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13909200513801948772">I mentally classify most novels into one of two broad categories: Literature or Crap. Within the Crap category there are several further levels. Books with negligible literary attributes (like no plot, no character development, poor writing, etc....ehh hmmm... Twilight) fall into the "Watching TV" category (because reading one of these books is the intellectual equivalent and takes the same amount of effort as sitting through a TV show). Marian Keyes' books definitely do not fall into the Litera</span>
  <span id="freeText13909200513801948772" style="display:none">I mentally classify most novels into one of two broad categories: Literature or Crap. Within the Crap category there are several further levels. Books with negligible literary attributes (like no plot, no character development, poor writing, etc....ehh hmmm... Twilight) fall into the "Watching TV" category (because reading one of these books is the intellectual equivalent and takes the same amount of effort as sitting through a TV show). Marian Keyes' books definitely do not fall into the Literature category because they don't offer much in the way of new insights or artistic use of language, but as far as Crap goes, they are pretty high quality. They are extremely funny and the writing is surprisingly GOOD! I definitely couldn't write that well while maintaining such a complexity of characters and plot lines for 600 pages. That's for sure. <br /><br />Her books are belittlingly labeled as "chick lit", forever dooming serious readers to deny having enjoyed them. But thinking about it, (and in an effort to justify my own enjoyment,) the whole chick lit phenomenon is remarkably anti-feminist. Why is there no equivalent nomen for books about traditionally testosterone-y topics like war, fist fights and cars ("dick lit" or "prick lit" are two possible suggestions - no more vulgar than "chick lit" mind you)? Personally, I'd much rather lose myself in a book about a peaceful topic like human relationships (romantic, familial or professional) and the beauty industry, than something bloody and violent. The fact that I am capable of losing myself in 600 pages about cosmetics, a topic that I know absolutely nothing about and have no interest in, is testament to the quality and pace of the writing and the story. Three stars instead of four because, without giving anything away, parts of the theme were really depressing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13909200513801948772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_31714663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31714663" />
    <a title="Bev" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1394428-bev"><img alt="Bev" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278947146p2/1394428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31714663?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bev" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bev" href="/user/show/1394428-bev">Bev</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394428-bev?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31714663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2550918845041256532">I'd have to put this book in my list of top-ten favorites of all time! I picked up the book-on-tape version at the library and immediately fell in love with Marian Keyes. I had to get the print version to enjoy the story again, and I am not usually one to re-read books (because there are so many others on my "to-read" list)! <br/><br/>After reading this most engaging novel, I felt compelled to read all of Keyes' other books, most of which were wonderful as well. This one remains my favorite of hers, howev</span>
  <span id="freeText2550918845041256532" style="display:none">I'd have to put this book in my list of top-ten favorites of all time! I picked up the book-on-tape version at the library and immediately fell in love with Marian Keyes. I had to get the print version to enjoy the story again, and I am not usually one to re-read books (because there are so many others on my "to-read" list)! <br /><br />After reading this most engaging novel, I felt compelled to read all of Keyes' other books, most of which were wonderful as well. This one remains my favorite of hers, however. I think it is several steps above the chick-lit category. The story is both hysterically funny and extremely poignant. I loved getting to know the Walsh sisters and bits and pieces of their various stories, so I was delighted to learn that there were other books that had different Walsh sisters as the main character.<br /><br />I like how Anna's story is revealed a little bit at a time, and the intermittent flashbacks that help us learn about her relationship to Aiden. I fell in love with him right along with her and felt endeared to him throughout the story. I sobbed at the end--it was such a touching and satisfying conclusion. I enjoyed this book so much that I have given it as a gift to several of my friends. *Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2550918845041256532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_44549604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44549604" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1504452-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220820403p2/1504452.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2213214697370163904">This was my first Marian Keyes book, so I haven't read the others about the Walsh sisters. I think I have a hard time getting into a lot of books, it usually takes the first 100 pages before I care about the book. Once I hit the turning point in the novel (around chapter 25) it was un-put-down-able.   <span id="freeText2213214697370163904" style="display:none">This was my first Marian Keyes book, so I haven't read the others about the Walsh sisters. I think I have a hard time getting into a lot of books, it usually takes the first 100 pages before I care about the book. Once I hit the turning point in the novel (around chapter 25) it was un-put-down-able. Seriously, I read the majority of the book on Sunday afternoon (about 300 pages).<br /><br />I enjoy Anna, there is a lot that I can relate to about her under the surface. She is a PR Account Executive, I've worked in the PR field (not on the account side) for about five years and the things she would complain about made me giggle because I could totally see it.<br /><br />Watching Anna remember February 16th was heartbreaking, watching her recovery would break my heart one minute and have me laughing out loud the next page. Definitely a good read, now I think I need to read Watermelon so I can experience more of the other Walsh sisters. Only Helen and Rachel were discussed a lot in Anybody Out There?</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21343573" />
    <a title="Krystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/110181-krystal"><img alt="Krystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180720905p2/110181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21343573?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystal" href="/user/show/110181-krystal">Krystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/110181-krystal?shelf=chicklit">chicklit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/110181-krystal?shelf=variousfemaleauthors">variousfemaleauthors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21343573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6779771671416035424">I'm having a love affair with Keyes at the moment. Started with Lucy Sullivan gets married (loved it) hiccuped with Watermelon (not so much) then on to Rachel's holiday (rivaled Lucy's story) and now, this one. Anybody out there is Anna's story. Keyes was on point in this book, Anna was heartbreakingly familiar. When I realized where her story was heading I was a bit angry, as I was already in love with Anna and Andy as a couple...how could Keyes do this to me. It was the delicate way that Keyes</span>
  <span id="freeText6779771671416035424" style="display:none">I'm having a love affair with Keyes at the moment. Started with Lucy Sullivan gets married (loved it) hiccuped with Watermelon (not so much) then on to Rachel's holiday (rivaled Lucy's story) and now, this one. Anybody out there is Anna's story. Keyes was on point in this book, Anna was heartbreakingly familiar. When I realized where her story was heading I was a bit angry, as I was already in love with Anna and Andy as a couple...how could Keyes do this to me. It was the delicate way that Keyes wove Annas story that made me keep reading through my anger =) <br /><br />I love how in each of these story about this family, one sisters life story, or segment of their life, is explored, and then you kind of get updates in the following sisters story. It's a nice way for the stories to continue. <br /><br />I'm trying not to give too much away, mostly cause I know Laura has this marked as to read. There were many moments in the books where I just paused and was wowed by Keyes ability to turn a phrase, or make a moment so recognizable and emotional. <br /><br />One of my favorite quotes (cause I have felt this way before) is<br /><br />"Funnily enough, I wasn't that keen on butterflies. It was a hard thing to admit because everyone loves butterflies and not liking them is akin to saying you don't like Michael Palin, or dolphins or strawberries. But to me, butterflies were slightly sneaky; all they were were moths in embroidered jackets. And, yes, moths were creepy and their flapping wings made a nasty papery sound-but at least they were honest; they were brown, they were dull, they were stupid (flying into flames at the drop of a hat). All in all, they hadn't much going for them but they didn't pretend to be anything other than what they were."<br /><br />its not really a pivotal quote, but I liked it ;)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6779771671416035424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/388792-jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6358603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9384428405733991709">I read the Marian Keyes novels completely out of order, having started with a copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46182.In_Watermelon_Sugar' title='In Watermelon Sugar by Richard Brautigan' rel='nofollow noopener'> Watermelon</a> my mum leant me when I was home on break. As a result, I perhaps saw the Sullivan girls mature in a slightly different order than other people who read the books in "order."<br/><br/>Nevertheless, I was confused by this book, and one other, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9301.Rachel_s_Holiday__Walsh_Family___2_' title='Rachel's Holiday (Walsh Family, #2) by Marian Keyes' rel='nofollow noopener'> Rachel's Holiday</a>. From the initial character development I got on Anna and Rachel, I always felt that it would have made far more sense to send Anna to rehab. <br/><br/>This book w</span>
  <span id="freeText9384428405733991709" style="display:none">I read the Marian Keyes novels completely out of order, having started with a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46182.In_Watermelon_Sugar" title="In Watermelon Sugar by Richard Brautigan" rel="nofollow noopener"> Watermelon</a> my mum leant me when I was home on break. As a result, I perhaps saw the Sullivan girls mature in a slightly different order than other people who read the books in "order."<br /><br />Nevertheless, I was confused by this book, and one other, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9301.Rachel_s_Holiday__Walsh_Family___2_" title="Rachel's Holiday (Walsh Family, #2) by Marian Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rachel's Holiday</a>. From the initial character development I got on Anna and Rachel, I always felt that it would have made far more sense to send Anna to rehab. <br /><br />This book was even further for me. This isn't a bad book. The writing isn't bad, although the plot is a bit strange. My main complaint about this novel is that, for my money, except for a few small flashbacks that fill in the missing years between books, this novel has NOTHING to do with the Anna we meet in the other books. Pretty much all of the Anna, the pretty, somewhat diaphanous hippie we meet in the other books-- is explained away in a few pages, which sum up a whirlwind of her life and dismiss every other instance of her in the series. I felt discomfited by this fact, especially since I felt that the actions of the character in this novel were not in tune with those which would have been taken by the character I knew. <br /><br />All in all, I felt if Keyes felt she needed to write this book, it should have been written as a stand-alone; I didn't feel the plot was well-served by being compressed into a standing character structure that really did not allow for the interplay between the characters here. If nothing else, again, I feel this book would have been better "delegated" to Rachel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9384428405733991709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

One was with Remember Me? and the other one was with this great one by Marion Keyes.   <span id="freeText5043075158609086672" style="display:none">SPOILERS AHEAD - do not read if you plan to read this book!!<br /><br />I've had a sense of deja vu lately when I've been reading. One was with Remember Me? and the other one was with this great one by Marion Keyes. It's been ages since I read PS I Love You by Cecilia Ahern but I think the premise was similar - in this one, the main character has been seriously injured in a car crash that has killed her newlywed husband. She is in denial of this fact for the first third of the book but then comes to accept it and is in grim pursuit of trying to communicate with him, along with dealing with her friends sympathy and trying to keep her job at a cosmetics firm. I loved it - she's an Irish woman living in NYC and her family back in Dublin is hilarious, and the twist at the end of the book brings it to a satisfying conclusion. I don't think I've ever been let down by Marion Keyes. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7601886972914416666">This wasn't quite as bad as I thought it would be, but it was not the kind of book I would ever have picked up on my own. <div id="review_150379732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150379732" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150379732?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hildy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hildy" href="/user/show/5033175-hildy">Hildy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150379732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11772493503525340896">first read: February 2011<br/>second read: December 2016<br/><br/>This is one of my favourite books. It is rare that I read about a couple that is so obviously perfect for each other and so intensely in love. I miss that. This book is quirky, laugh out loud funny, and so emotional. Keyes nailed every part of this. It was long but I still wish that there was more to read.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_71767677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71767677" />
    <a title="Alisha Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1585205-alisha-marie"><img alt="Alisha Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555610435p2/1585205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71767677?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisha Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisha Marie" href="/user/show/1585205-alisha-marie">Alisha Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1585205-alisha-marie?shelf=books-i-own-that-i-ve-read">books-i-own-that-i-ve-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1585205-alisha-marie?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1585205-alisha-marie?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71767677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1997954566396483973">Anybody Out There was a book that started out really great. However, after a while, not only did it start to drag on, it also started to resemble a mess...a mildly intriguing mess, but a mess none the less. Now, I don't need much from a chick-lit to be happy, but in Anybody Out There, I just needed more.<br/><br/>The Good: Part 1. Part 1 of Anybody Out There was the best out of the three parts in this book. The family dynamics, which was my favorite part of Anybody Out There, were more prominent in the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText1997954566396483973" style="display:none">Anybody Out There was a book that started out really great. However, after a while, not only did it start to drag on, it also started to resemble a mess...a mildly intriguing mess, but a mess none the less. Now, I don't need much from a chick-lit to be happy, but in Anybody Out There, I just needed more.<br /><br />The Good: Part 1. Part 1 of Anybody Out There was the best out of the three parts in this book. The family dynamics, which was my favorite part of Anybody Out There, were more prominent in the first part and were only alluded to in the last two parts. Another good thing was the twist. I definitely did not see that coming, particularly because I thought this was going to be a breezy, easy, funny chick-lit. Definite points for the twist.<br /><br />The Okay: Part 3. Part 3, where everything was coming together, was not as good as Part 1, but way better than Part 2. Jacqui's side plot was funny enough that it kept me interested in Anybody Out There. As unplausible as it was, I was also mildly satisfied with the ending. Although, that could have been because I just wanted the book to be over.<br /><br />The Bad: Part 2. I don't know how something involving mediums could've been so flippin' boring. Part 2 just dragged on and on. Oh, and Helen's emails...also dragged on and on. I found Helen to be funny and interesting at first, but after those emails, I was so incredibly bored with her character. That side plot was just pointless. Another bad thing about Anybody Out There was the numerous side plots. You had the mediums, you had the husband turmoil, the job turmoil, the ex-girlfriend turmoil, and a couple more turmoils that I don't feel like elaborating on. This book just had way too much going on. Oh, and it also stopped being funny at one point.<br /> <br />So, overall, I found Anybody Out There to be a dud. No laugh out loud moments, but a couple of chuckles at first. Then, there were no chuckles...no type of laughter. There was major eye-rolling, though. Utterly forgettable and more than a little boring, so I say skip it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1997954566396483973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_39468027" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39468027" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/236648-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282693240p2/236648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39468027?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/236648-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who aren't already sad enough</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jen by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1473508-gg">Gg</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=rough-read">rough-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=irish">irish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=love-hurts">love-hurts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39468027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3295274010046422642">I love the various Marian Keyes books, especially the ones featuring the individual sisters from the Irish family, the Walshes. Her books are almost standard chick-lit fare, but Keyes's writing and her doses of Irish wickedness make them stand above the crowd.<br/><br/>This book features the fourth Walsh sister, Anna. We've met Anna in the other Walsh sister books, where she's something of a spacey, hippie-ish waif, but here she's been transformed into a savvy New York business woman--a bit of a stretch, </span>
  <span id="freeText3295274010046422642" style="display:none">I love the various Marian Keyes books, especially the ones featuring the individual sisters from the Irish family, the Walshes. Her books are almost standard chick-lit fare, but Keyes's writing and her doses of Irish wickedness make them stand above the crowd.<br /><br />This book features the fourth Walsh sister, Anna. We've met Anna in the other Walsh sister books, where she's something of a spacey, hippie-ish waif, but here she's been transformed into a savvy New York business woman--a bit of a stretch, I thought, but, hey, I was glad Anna seemed to have pulled herself together. All the other books deal with some type of major upheaval in the heroines' lives, but Anna gets nailed the worst, I think. This one still had funny moments, but really, it was a pretty heavy read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3295274010046422642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3228315647" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10224855003258030682">Update to post with My Review: March 19th, 2020<br/><br/>For the second time recently, I have chosen to read a novel, that is part of a series, without realising until after I had finished! The first one in the Walsh family series was 'Water Melon' which I read in 1996, cannot recall the content now, neither have I read any of the others. Honestly, I do not feel this matters as it stands alone perfectly. A sad read but Marian Keyes has lifted the story with a lot of humour, so expect tears and laughs. Do </span>
  <span id="freeText10224855003258030682" style="display:none">Update to post with My Review: March 19th, 2020<br /><br />For the second time recently, I have chosen to read a novel, that is part of a series, without realising until after I had finished! The first one in the Walsh family series was 'Water Melon' which I read in 1996, cannot recall the content now, neither have I read any of the others. Honestly, I do not feel this matters as it stands alone perfectly. A sad read but Marian Keyes has lifted the story with a lot of humour, so expect tears and laughs. Do not be put off by the nearly 600 pages as it is a very quick read, that will take you out of yourself. Something we all need in these difficult times. <br /><br />Pre Read Notes: March 12th, 2020<br />I am going to start this today; I don't think I read the earlier ones in the Walsh family series so hope it doesn't matter?<br /><br />My intention had been to start Grown Ups but finding this sitting on my TBR shelf, thought I should read this older title first! Originally published in 2006 and republished in 2012, this period was when I was living in Italy and did not get to read any books written by Marian Keyes. In fact, I rediscovered her work in 2017 when I read 'The Break' and reviewed on LindyLouMac's Book Reviews, prior to this I have not read any novels by her since 2001. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://lindyloumacbookreviews.blogspot.com/2018/05/the-break-by-marian-keyes.html">https://lindyloumacbookreviews.blogsp...</a><br /><br />#bookreviews #authors #MarianKeyes</span>

<div id="review_26555457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26555457" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1304553-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339540125p2/1304553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26555457?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1304553-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060731304" href="/book/show/9299.Anybody_Out_There_">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26555457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8381789428042562992">This is a story about one of the Walsh sisters. There are five sisters in this Irish family that Marian Keyes has written several books about. This one is about Anna. It begins with her in in Ireland at her parents' home, although we find out early that she lives in New York and is here recovering. We also know that she misses Aidan very much and that she feels she must recover from her injuries quickly so that she can get back to New York to find him. What we do not know is what happened to her</span>
  <span id="freeText8381789428042562992" style="display:none">This is a story about one of the Walsh sisters. There are five sisters in this Irish family that Marian Keyes has written several books about. This one is about Anna. It begins with her in in Ireland at her parents' home, although we find out early that she lives in New York and is here recovering. We also know that she misses Aidan very much and that she feels she must recover from her injuries quickly so that she can get back to New York to find him. What we do not know is what happened to her or where Aidan has gone. Her family does not want her to go back and tries to protect her from whatever is waiting for her there. Anna has to face the past in order to move on though. The story is told in flashbacks and is touching and funny. The Walsh family had me laughing out loud, while the Anna's story had me in tears. I highly recommend this title as I enjoyed it very much. If you like this book, try Keyes' other novels about the Walsh's.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8381789428042562992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2874456233" />
    <a title="Melinda Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3101703-melinda-elizabeth"><img alt="Melinda Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449296084p2/3101703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2874456233?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda Elizabeth" href="/user/show/3101703-melinda-elizabeth">Melinda Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2874456233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16317968004523078914">whoops I did it again, read a book half way through a series I didn't know existed... but the best part is that you definitely didn't need any prior knowledge of the Walsh family to enjoy this one! <br/><br/>Anna is in Dublin recuperating. We are given details sparingly about what is wrong with her and how it happened, and we aren't too sure what is going on with her husband Aidan. Is she stalking him? Are they talking? Why is he ignoring her when she gets back to New York? <br/><br/>Split into three parts, Anybody</span>
  <span id="freeText16317968004523078914" style="display:none">whoops I did it again, read a book half way through a series I didn't know existed... but the best part is that you definitely didn't need any prior knowledge of the Walsh family to enjoy this one! <br /><br />Anna is in Dublin recuperating. We are given details sparingly about what is wrong with her and how it happened, and we aren't too sure what is going on with her husband Aidan. Is she stalking him? Are they talking? Why is he ignoring her when she gets back to New York? <br /><br />Split into three parts, Anybody Out There has very distinct parts that make the book easy to read and keeps you interested in the story. There's some great comedic moments throughout and a nice love story at its heart. If you have read the others in the series I'm sure this one fits right in, if not then it's also fine to read by itself.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2287744547?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen" href="/user/show/1661766-colleen">Colleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2287744547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14523477007436973433">One of the reviewers of this book said she classifies books into either literature or crap. I would probably call the second category "fluff" instead. The reviewer also mentions there are levels within the categories. So true. This book is "fluff" but it has some good messages about the difficulty of the grieving process. For about a third of the book, we don't know why Anna Walsh has been injured or why her husband doesn't seem to be responding to her. We experience her crazy family and friends</span>
  <span id="freeText14523477007436973433" style="display:none">One of the reviewers of this book said she classifies books into either literature or crap. I would probably call the second category "fluff" instead. The reviewer also mentions there are levels within the categories. So true. This book is "fluff" but it has some good messages about the difficulty of the grieving process. For about a third of the book, we don't know why Anna Walsh has been injured or why her husband doesn't seem to be responding to her. We experience her crazy family and friends throughout; they are all a bit over the top. Anna goes over the top a few times as well. The author could probably have cut out about 100 pages and still told the story. But, with that said, I may read more of Marian Keyes "fluff" especially in the Walsh family series. Her "fluff" provides some relief from more serious books/literature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14523477007436973433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780718147648" href="/book/show/848757.Anybody_Out_There_">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107623426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14057933244434630654">I enjoyed this book as I do with most of Marian Keyes' books. I agree though with my daughter Samantha, who read this book first and said she enjoyed it, but the story was a bit depressing. (Even Marian Keyes agreed!) I felt I knew the characters fairly well as they have been in a few of the books I have read by the same author. The family is quite big and lots of different things are going on all the time.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UWox+gMLBAtTw1eGrsiArZWuqy6bFd3YqpbTwUgQUlapmt6xWBdvUwk0oyd66Xh67aJfz+dJFoe12Fs/sPV2nA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KcRojbueH/ohKkoJ7kbvFqkeuf9bEjnUXUON0Z9Bn/PRNIfG4IJ0onvdvqg6ZxfB0RJNHidO8otCDQUvZ6S7OQ==')})

<span id="freeTextContainer583844757047093080">Marian Keyes (born 10 September 1963) is an Irish novelist and non-fiction writer, best known for her work in women's literature. She is an Irish Book Awards winner. Over 22 million copies of her novels have been sold worldwide and her books have been translated into 32 languages. She became known worldwide for <i>Watermelon</i>, <i>Lucy Sullivan is Getting Married</i>, and <i>This Charming Man</i>, with themes includ</span>
  <span id="freeText583844757047093080" style="display:none">Marian Keyes (born 10 September 1963) is an Irish novelist and non-fiction writer, best known for her work in women's literature. She is an Irish Book Awards winner. Over 22 million copies of her novels have been sold worldwide and her books have been translated into 32 languages. She became known worldwide for <i>Watermelon</i>, <i>Lucy Sullivan is Getting Married</i>, and <i>This Charming Man</i>, with themes including domestic violence and alcoholism.<br /></span>
